Salut ph-m,

it seems that you can't assign a default value to reference parameters
(cf. http://fr2.php.net/manual/fr/language.references.pass.php#56644)
this is why you got your error when calling YDAjax constructor
function in line 68 of YDAjax.php...

Amicalement
po?

PS: En clair, dans une d?finition, tu ne peux pas initialiser un
argument pass? par r?f?rence ;-)

From francisco at fusemail.com  Thu Mar  2 00:33:39 2006
From: francisco at fusemail.com (Francisco Azevedo)
Date: Wed, 01 Mar 2006 23:33:39 +0000
Subject: [ydf-users] Ajax Error
In-Reply-To: <829084a60603011002p405effeao@mail.gmail.com>
References: <829084a60603010523o28413e3an@mail.gmail.com>	 <306340e00603010924o1cc39243w@mail.gmail.com> <829084a60603011002p405effeao@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <44062F53.9090904@fusemail.com>

Hi ph-m

> it's seems it's in YDAjax.php script, cause when I test Ajax examples
> with last release 1755, all fail.
> 
> I try at home and I got this in my apache log error :
> 
> [Wed Mar 01 18:58:28 2006] [error] PHP Parse error:  parse error,
> unexpected '=', expecting ')' in
> e:\\wamp\\htdocs\\www\\ydf2\\YDFramework2\\addons\\YDAjax\\YDAjax.php
> on line 68

Yes, the problem is in YDAjax (well.. is more a php4 problem to me). On 
php5 (my development version) everything went fine.

I had changed that because the form element is not really required. 
Sometimes we don't need a form.. but we want to use YDAjax. So we need a 
default value (null) for a form.
Another problem is when we have more than one YDForm. Currently we don't 
have a way to add YDForms to YDAjax.. we can just use one. So, we have 2 
problems here.

Your problem can be solved easily (because you are not using YDAjax 
without the form)...
But i'm planing to delete this parameter and YDAjax will have only the 
$template variable. Then, a new method will be added to YDAjax to add 
form elements. This way, we can have zero, one or more YDForms in 
YDAjax. This latest feature is planned but it's not trivial to implement 
because there are lots of form elements searches inside YDAjax.

Francisco

From dab214 at yahoo.com  Tue Mar  7 19:54:23 2006
From: dab214 at yahoo.com (dab)
Date: Tue, 7 Mar 2006 10:54:23 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [ydf-users] YDDatabaseObject numeric arrays
Message-ID: <20060307185423.40329.qmail@web50202.mail.yahoo.com>

hi all,
i remember there was a forum thread about this before.
can't get below code to fetch a numeric array.
it works fine in YDDatabase but not in
YDDatabaseObject. Sorry in advance if this has been
covered somewhere else :/


YDConfig::set( 'YD_DB_FETCHTYPE', YD_DB_FETCH_NUM );
$user = YDDatabaseObject::getInstance('users');
$user->select ( 'username' );
$user->find();
$db = $user->getResults();

result:
Array
(
    [0] => Array
        (
            [username] => dab
        )

    [1] => Array
        (
            [username] => asdf
        )

)

From muitocomplicado at gmail.com  Tue Mar  7 20:59:59 2006
From: muitocomplicado at gmail.com (David Bittencourt)
Date: Tue, 7 Mar 2006 16:59:59 -0300
Subject: [ydf-users] YDDatabaseObject numeric arrays
In-Reply-To: <20060307185423.40329.qmail@web50202.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20060307185423.40329.qmail@web50202.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <12260be20603071159x17f1093dre9dcde369bee8654@mail.gmail.com>

That will not work indeed.

YDDatabaseObject always returns an associative array because it must fill
the object with the values and there's a $user->username and not $user->0.

But I think that you just want something like this, right?

array (
0 => 'dab',
1 => 'asdf',
)

Try getResultsAsAssocArray and forget about setting YDConfig::set(
'YD_DB_FETCHTYPE', YD_DB_FETCH_NUM );

$arr = $user->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'key', 'username' );

You must pass a key or the function will automatically try to use all
registered keys in the class.

-db

> 0 => 'dab',
> 1 => 'asdf',
> )
> 
> Try getResultsAsAssocArray and forget about setting
> YDConfig::set(
> 'YD_DB_FETCHTYPE', YD_DB_FETCH_NUM );
> 
> $arr = $user->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'key',
> 'username' );
> 
> You must pass a key or the function will
> automatically try to use all
> registered keys in the class.
> 
> -db
> 
> 
> On 3/7/06, dab <dab214 at yahoo.com> wrote:
> >

> before.

> been
> > covered somewhere else :/

> );

> > $user->find();
> > $db = $user->getResults();

From dab214 at yahoo.com  Wed Mar  8 15:19:07 2006
From: dab214 at yahoo.com (dab)
Date: Wed, 8 Mar 2006 06:19:07 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [ydf-users] YDAjax autocompleter
In-Reply-To: <3fb044fd0603071227w20379bb6m698506742018790f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20060308141907.9248.qmail@web50203.mail.yahoo.com>

hi all,
i use the autocomplete function on quite a lot of
fields so it would be better if i could pass the table
and field name to the ajax method so i don't have to
write one extra method for each element.
by looking at the YDFormElement_Autocompleter below
code should work, but it doesn't :(

$this->form->addElement ( 'autocompleter',
'firstname', 'First Name:', $this->attributes, array(
&$this, 'getAjaxElement', array ( 'affiliate',
'firstname' ) ) );

function getAjaxElement ( $text ) {
    $info = $this->getAjaxArguments();
    $table = $info[0];
    $field = $info[1];
    $user = YDDatabaseObject::getInstance ( $table );
    $user->select ( 'id', $field );
    $user->find();
    $db = $user->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'id', $field
);
	$result = array();
	foreach( $db as $key => $el )
		if (eregi("^". $text ."+", $el)) $result[] = $el;
		
	$this->ajax->addCompleterResult( $result ); 
	return $this->ajax->processResults();           
}

Hi dab.

My first look at your code is telling me that you are defining an 
autocompleter with 'getAjaxElement' and 2 arguments.. but on your 
'getAjaxElement' you only set 1 argument ($text).

You should try:

function getAjaxElement ( $affiliate, $firstname ) {
    ...
}

Francisco A

From francisco at fusemail.com  Thu Mar  9 23:49:55 2006
From: francisco at fusemail.com (Francisco Azevedo)
Date: Thu, 09 Mar 2006 22:49:55 +0000
Subject: [ydf-users] YDAjax autocompleter
In-Reply-To: <20060309141837.84325.qmail@web50207.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20060309141837.84325.qmail@web50207.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4410B113.90403@fusemail.com>

Hi dab

The solution for your problem is exactly what i said on my last email.
Please not that:

1 - You should define all arguments in a array (when adding a 
autocompleter to a form)

2 - You should define the same quantity of arguments in the server function.

3 - You should NOT use any of the YDFormElement_Autocompleter methods

So..

1:
$this->form->addElement( 'autocompleter', 'firstname', 'First Name:', 
$this->attributes, array( &$this, 'getAjaxElement', array( 'affiliate', 
'firstname' ) ) );

2:
function getAjaxElement ( $affiliate, $firstname ) {
      ...
}


Francisco A

From maximus_meridius79 at yahoo.com  Fri Mar 10 15:55:20 2006
From: maximus_meridius79 at yahoo.com (maximus meridius)
Date: Fri, 10 Mar 2006 06:55:20 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [ydf-users] YDajax - clean the HTML with Behaviour
Message-ID: <20060310145520.43693.qmail@web53801.mail.yahoo.com>

    Hi,

I've spent the last couple of nights trying out YDajax. I'm quiteimpressed as it integrates nicely with YDF. I thought it would be niceto remove the dependency on YDform.

One improvement would be to make use of the Behaviour library fromhttp://bennolan.com/behaviour/ . This allows the resulting HTML to bequite clean since the resulting HTML does not have javascript eventattributes. This is BSD licensed.

Another toy to look at for rich AJAX affects is Rico (http://openrico.org/rico/home.page ). This is apache licensed.

The only downside to adding these things is of course bloat.

Regards,

Graeme

Bring photos to life! New PhotoMail  makes sharing a breeze.

From francisco at fusemail.com  Sun Mar 12 18:12:17 2006
From: francisco at fusemail.com (Francisco Azevedo)
Date: Sun, 12 Mar 2006 17:12:17 +0000
Subject: [ydf-users] YDajax - clean the HTML with Behaviour
In-Reply-To: <20060310145520.43693.qmail@web53801.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20060310145520.43693.qmail@web53801.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <44145671.8020002@fusemail.com>

Hi maximus meridius

> I've spent the last couple of nights trying out YDajax. I'm quite 
> impressed as it integrates nicely with YDF. I thought it would be nice 
> to remove the dependency on YDform.

As you said in other email, since v2.4, YDForm object is not required 
anymore... but it's recommended ;)
 From that version it's possible to use YDAjax without the form logic 
_and_ it's possible to use up to 10 YDForms at the same time too :)


> One improvement would be to make use of the Behaviour library from 
> http://bennolan.com/behaviour/ . This allows the resulting HTML to be 
> quite clean since the resulting HTML does not have javascript event 
> attributes. This is BSD licensed.

I saw that but i think, in some complex cases, it can be ugly.
As YDAjax is created now, it works very well when you use YDForms 
(because you don't need to care about the js generated) and when you 
just add custom events (because you only need to care about the js 
function name, everything else is done by YDAjax).

> Another toy to look at for rich AJAX affects is Rico ( 
> http://openrico.org/rico/home.page ). This is apache licensed.

OpenRico seems very powerful. the only problem i see is that it's a pack 
of different features.. ajax, effects, drag&drop..
As you know, in YDF you have YDAjax (that is integrated with a effect 
lib too). ;)

Francisco A

From dab214 at yahoo.com  Mon Mar 13 19:48:34 2006
From: dab214 at yahoo.com (dab)

hi francisco,
i had 1778 too and reversed it to 1775 and it works
now. i have PHP Version 5.1.1.

and maybe i can't do what i'm trying to do, none of
the examples does what i want to do :(
i use the autocompleter a lot across the site so it
would be good to use the same function for all
autocompleter elements (by passing arguments on each
element instead of writing a function for each
element).

the below code works, but i want set the field and
table variables with values passed as arguments.

do you think this is possible with current ydajax
functionality?

function getElement( $text ){

    $field = 'firstname';
    $table = 'user';

    $dbo = YDDatabaseObject::getInstance ( $table );
    $dbo->select ( 'id', $field );
    $dbo->find();
    $db = $dbo->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'id', $field
);

	// initialize result array
	$result = array();
	
	// check db for text matches and store them in result
array
	foreach( $db as $el )
		if (eregi("^". $text ."+", $el)) $result[] = $el;

	// assign result to current completer (YDAjax
automagically detects the autocompleter that made this
call)
	$this->ajax->addCompleterResult( $result );

	// return response to client browser
	return $this->ajax->processResults();
}

> dab
> 
> If you want functions you cannot add events to form
> elements. You must 
> create the js function.

> Second, you have 3 types of arguments that you can
> pass on addEvent:
> - form element names
> - static string/int/float values
> - dynamic js arguments from the function
>

> events added as

From francisco at fusemail.com  Mon Mar 13 22:12:39 2006
From: francisco at fusemail.com (Francisco Azevedo)
Date: Mon, 13 Mar 2006 21:12:39 +0000
Subject: [ydf-users] YDAjax autocompleter
In-Reply-To: <20060313184834.36526.qmail@web50204.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20060313184834.36526.qmail@web50204.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4415E047.3060602@fusemail.com>

hi dab

 > i had 1778 too and reversed it to 1775 and it works
 > now. i have PHP Version 5.1.1.


Sorry to disapoint you again but i don't have any problems with 1778 
(using php 5.1.2).

Is there someone, like dab, that cannot see the examples?

> and maybe i can't do what i'm trying to do, none of
> the examples does what i want to do :(
> i use the autocompleter a lot across the site so it
> would be good to use the same function for all
> autocompleter elements (by passing arguments on each
> element instead of writing a function for each
> element).

dab, each autocompleter has its own ajax call and you must define what 
do you want in that call. By default the autocompleter sends its content 
but you can define other arguments.
If you want to use 1 php server function for all autocompleters (like 
the autocompleter example where you have 2 autocompleters that send 
their contents to a shared php function) and you want to know (inside 
the php function) what autocompleter made the ajax call you can, eg, 
define in each autocompleter call some static values that define the 
field and table.

$form->addElement('autocompleter_1', 'a1', 'label', '', array( &$this, 
'getElement', array( 'a1', '1, 'firstname1', 'user1' ) );

$form->addElement('autocompleter_2', 'a2', 'label', '', array( &$this, 
'getElement', array( 'a2', '2', 'firstnameX', 'userX' ) );

$form->addElement('autocompleter_3', 'a3', 'label', '', array( &$this, 
'getElement', array( 'a3', '3', 'firstnameZ', 'userZ' ) );

then you only need to define the php function like:

function getElement( $autocompleterContent, $id, $field, $table ){

      $dbo = YDDatabaseObject::getInstance ( $table );
      $dbo->select ( 'id', $field );
      $dbo->find();
      $db = $dbo->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'id', $field );

      // initialize result array
      $result = array();
  	
      // check db for text matches and store them in result
      foreach( $db as $el )
         if (eregi("^". $text ."+", $el)) $result[] = $el;

      // assign result to current completer
      $this->ajax->addCompleterResult( $result );

      // return response to client browser
      return $this->ajax->processResults();
}

as you will see getElement will get:
- autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstname1' string + 'user1' 
string.. when call is made from 'a1'

- autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstnameX' string + 'userX' 
string.. when call is made from 'a2'

- autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstnameZ' string + 'userZ' 
string.. when call is made from 'a3'


.. and if you inspect the code, YDAjax will try to reuse functions.

Francisco A

From muitocomplicado at gmail.com  Tue Mar 14 21:59:15 2006
From: muitocomplicado at gmail.com (David Bittencourt)
Date: Tue, 14 Mar 2006 17:59:15 -0300
Subject: [ydf-users] query regarding database connection
In-Reply-To: <4aef63030603140745q496d8a66x994fc06bf804b1f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <20060314055840.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.7521b56b82.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
	 <4aef63030603140745q496d8a66x994fc06bf804b1f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <12260be20603141259w5ac8f855hcbc1e69671d88607@mail.gmail.com>

The thing is the getInstance method doesn't try to connect to the database.
It just set's the YDDatabaseDriver object with the parameters.

Only at the first query or calling directly the connect() method the
connection will be made or will trigger a fatal error if it wasn't able to
connect.

If you set the error_reporting level to not show any errors, then you will
not see if the connection was unsuccessful.

-db

From dab214 at yahoo.com  Fri Mar 17 21:31:09 2006
From: dab214 at yahoo.com (dab)
Date: Fri, 17 Mar 2006 12:31:09 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [ydf-users] how to pass value to textarea in the template page  from php page
In-Reply-To: <20060317054229.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.22fe18ddfa.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
Message-ID: <20060317203109.22810.qmail@web50202.mail.yahoo.com>

hi moses,
don't worry, it's really easy =)
i normally do something like this:

function actionWhatever() {
    //get some data
    $dbo = YDDatabaseObject::getInstance('whatever');
    $dbo->find();
    $results = $dbo->getResults();
    
    //now create the form and set the form values
    $form = YDForm ('whatever');
    $form->setDefaults ($results);

    $this->template->assignForm( 'whatever', $form ); 
    $this->template->display ( 'whatever.tpl' ); 

}

> > would be good to use the same function for all
> > autocompleter elements (by passing arguments on
> each
> > element instead of writing a function for each
> > element).
> 
> dab, each autocompleter has its own ajax call and
> you must define what 
> do you want in that call. By default the
> autocompleter sends its content 
> but you can define other arguments.
> If you want to use 1 php server function for all
> autocompleters (like 
> the autocompleter example where you have 2
> autocompleters that send 
> their contents to a shared php function) and you
> want to know (inside 
> the php function) what autocompleter made the ajax
> call you can, eg, 
> define in each autocompleter call some static values
> that define the 
> field and table.
> 
> $form->addElement('autocompleter_1', 'a1', 'label',
> '', array( &$this, 
> 'getElement', array( 'a1', '1, 'firstname1', 'user1'
> ) );
> 
> $form->addElement('autocompleter_2', 'a2', 'label',
> '', array( &$this, 
> 'getElement', array( 'a2', '2', 'firstnameX',
> 'userX' ) );
> 
> $form->addElement('autocompleter_3', 'a3', 'label',
> '', array( &$this, 
> 'getElement', array( 'a3', '3', 'firstnameZ',
> 'userZ' ) );
> 
> then you only need to define the php function like:
> 
> function getElement( $autocompleterContent, $id,
> $field, $table ){
> 
>       $dbo = YDDatabaseObject::getInstance ( $table
> );
>       $dbo->select ( 'id', $field );
>       $dbo->find();
>       $db = $dbo->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'id',
> $field );
> 
>       // initialize result array
>       $result = array();
>   	
>       // check db for text matches and store them in
> result
>       foreach( $db as $el )
>          if (eregi("^". $text ."+", $el)) $result[]
> = $el;
> 
>       // assign result to current completer
>       $this->ajax->addCompleterResult( $result );
> 
>       // return response to client browser
>       return $this->ajax->processResults();
> }
> 
> as you will see getElement will get:
> - autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstname1'
> string + 'user1' 
> string.. when call is made from 'a1'
> 
> - autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstnameX'
> string + 'userX' 
> string.. when call is made from 'a2'
> 
> - autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstnameZ'
> string + 'userZ' 
> string.. when call is made from 'a3'
> 
> 
> .. and if you inspect the code, YDAjax will try to
> reuse functions.
> 
> Francisco A
> 
> > the below code works, but i want set the field and
> > table variables with values passed as arguments.
> > 
> > do you think this is possible with current ydajax
> > functionality?
> > 
> > function getElement( $text ){
> > 
> >     $field = 'firstname';

> >     $dbo->find();
> >     $db = $dbo->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'id',
> $field
> > );
> >

> > 	$result = array();
> >

> result
> > array
> > 	foreach( $db as $el )
> > 		if (eregi("^". $text ."+", $el)) $result[] =
> $el;
> > 
> > 	// assign result to current completer (YDAjax
> > automagically detects the autocompleter that made
> this
> > call)
> > 	$this->ajax->addCompleterResult( $result );
> > 
> > 	// return response to client browser
> > 	return $this->ajax->processResults();

> >>pass on addEvent:
> >>- form element names
> >>- static string/int/float values
> >>- dynamic js arguments from the function

> >>Remember that dynamic arguments can only be used

> >>So, if you want to make _one_ js function that
> sends

>>> i use the autocompleter a lot across the site so
>> it
>>> would be good to use the same function for all
>>> autocompleter elements (by passing arguments on
>> each
>>> element instead of writing a function for each
>>> element).
>> dab, each autocompleter has its own ajax call and
>> you must define what 
>> do you want in that call. By default the
>> autocompleter sends its content 
>> but you can define other arguments.
>> If you want to use 1 php server function for all
>> autocompleters (like 
>> the autocompleter example where you have 2
>> autocompleters that send 
>> their contents to a shared php function) and you
>> want to know (inside 
>> the php function) what autocompleter made the ajax
>> call you can, eg, 
>> define in each autocompleter call some static values
>> that define the 
>> field and table.
>>
>> $form->addElement('autocompleter_1', 'a1', 'label',
>> '', array( &$this, 
>> 'getElement', array( 'a1', '1, 'firstname1', 'user1'
>> ) );
>>
>> $form->addElement('autocompleter_2', 'a2', 'label',
>> '', array( &$this, 
>> 'getElement', array( 'a2', '2', 'firstnameX',
>> 'userX' ) );
>>
>> $form->addElement('autocompleter_3', 'a3', 'label',
>> '', array( &$this, 
>> 'getElement', array( 'a3', '3', 'firstnameZ',
>> 'userZ' ) );
>>
>> then you only need to define the php function like:
>>
>> function getElement( $autocompleterContent, $id,
>> $field, $table ){
>>
>>       $dbo = YDDatabaseObject::getInstance ( $table
>> );
>>       $dbo->select ( 'id', $field );
>>       $dbo->find();
>>       $db = $dbo->getResultsAsAssocArray( 'id',
>> $field );
>>
>>       // initialize result array
>>       $result = array();
>>   	
>>       // check db for text matches and store them in
>> result
>>       foreach( $db as $el )
>>          if (eregi("^". $text ."+", $el)) $result[]
>> = $el;
>>
>>       // assign result to current completer
>>       $this->ajax->addCompleterResult( $result );
>>
>>       // return response to client browser
>>       return $this->ajax->processResults();
>> }
>>
>> as you will see getElement will get:
>> - autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstname1'
>> string + 'user1' 
>> string.. when call is made from 'a1'
>>
>> - autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstnameX'
>> string + 'userX' 
>> string.. when call is made from 'a2'
>>
>> - autocompleter content + '1' string + 'firstnameZ'
>> string + 'userZ' 
>> string.. when call is made from 'a3'
>>
>>
>> .. and if you inspect the code, YDAjax will try to
>> reuse functions.
>>
>> Francisco A
>>

Hi Moses,

this is something on my todo list for YDFramework 3.

The problem with version 4 of PHP is that is quite difficult to build in
proper exception handling as PHP4 doesn't support throw/catch constructs.
PHP5 however does support these and will make it very straightforward to
handle situations like these.

There are some tricks we can do to emulate something like this in PHP4, but
it's very time consuming and not easy to do.

Cheers,


pieter

From pieter at yellowduck.be  Thu Mar 23 09:45:21 2006
From: pieter at yellowduck.be (Pieter Claerhout)
Date: Thu, 23 Mar 2006 09:45:21 +0100
Subject: [ydf-users] query regarding database (YDDatabse)
In-Reply-To: <20060323010614.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.3380817575.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
References: <20060323010614.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.3380817575.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
Message-ID: <4aef63030603230045o88df9bby54b298756f76e3ae@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Moses,

the following code example shows you how to do it. This is the PHP file:


<?php

    // Standard include
    include_once( dirname( __FILE__ ) . '/../YDFramework2/YDF2_init.php' );

    // Includes
    YDInclude( 'YDForm.php' );
    YDInclude( 'YDTemplate.php' );

    // Class definition
    class form_radiobutton extends YDRequest {

        // Class constructor
        function form_radiobutton() {
            $this->YDRequest();
        }

        // Default action
        function actionDefault() {

            // Create the form
            $form = new YDForm( 'form1' );

            // Add the radiobutton
            $form->addElement(
                'radio', 'sex', 'Sex:', array(), array( 'male' => 'Male',
'female' => 'Female' )
            );

            // Add the submit button
            $form->addElement( 'submit', 'btnSubmit', 'submit' );

            // Set the defaults
            $form->setDefaults( array( 'sex' => 'male' ) );

            // Add the template
            $tpl = new YDTemplate();

            // Add the form to the template
            $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );

            // Display the template
            $tpl->display();

        }

    }

    // Process the request
    YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );

?>
The template looks as follows:

{$form.tag}
    {$form.sex.html}
    {$form.btnSubmit.html}
{$form.endtag}

When you add a radiobutton, the 4th parameter in the addElement function is
an array with the values (the array keys) and the names of the values (the
array values).

You also shouldn't put the radiobutton element twice on the template as that
will give strange results.

Hope that makes it a little bit more clear.

cheers,


pieter

From pieter at yellowduck.be  Thu Mar 23 09:51:00 2006
From: pieter at yellowduck.be (Pieter Claerhout)
Date: Thu, 23 Mar 2006 09:51:00 +0100
Subject: [ydf-users] Regarding YD AddElements
In-Reply-To: <20060322211317.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.79b9074533.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
References: <20060322211317.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.79b9074533.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
Message-ID: <4aef63030603230051q4fe0acb6x74a16fa412eb71bf@mail.gmail.com>

Moses,

the attributes array translates directly to the HTML attributes of the HTML
that is generated for the element. Any HTML attribute can be specified in
this array. You should however avoid to specify special attributes such as
"id", "name" and "value" as they are handled internally by the YDForm class.

For the options array, it depends on which form element we are talking
about. Some require options, some don't. The example "form2.php" should give
you an idea of which elements require options and which ones don't.

I will try to add this information to the user guide one day.

Cheers,


pieter

-------- Original Message --------
Subject: Re:[ydf-users] query regarding database
(YDDatabse)
From: "PieterClaerhout" <pieter at yellowduck.be>
Date: Thu, March 23, 20061:45 am
To:
"moses at softwaysolutions.com"<moses at softwaysolutions.com>,
ydframework-users at berlios.de

Hi Moses,
 
the following code example shows you how to do it.
This is the PHPfile:
 
<?php
    // Standard include
   include_once( dirname( __FILE__ ) .
'/../YDFramework2/YDF2_init.php');
    // Includes
    YDInclude('YDForm.php' );
    YDInclude( 'YDTemplate.php');
    // Class definition
    classform_radiobutton extends YDRequest {
        // Classconstructor
        functionform_radiobutton(){
           $this->YDRequest();
       }
        // Defaultaction
        functionactionDefault() {
            //Create theform
           $form = new YDForm( 'form1' );
            //Add theradiobutton
           $form->addElement(
               'radio', 'sex', 'Sex:', array(), array(
'male' => 'Male', 'female'=> 'Female')
           );
            //Add the submitbutton
           $form->addElement( 'submit', 'btnSubmit',
'submit' );
            //Set thedefaults
           $form->setDefaults( array( 'sex' => 'male'
) );
            //Add thetemplate
           $tpl = new YDTemplate();
            //Add the form to thetemplate
           $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );
            //Display thetemplate
           $tpl->display();
        }
    }
    // Process the request
   YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );
?>
The template looks as follows:
 
{$form.tag}
   {$form.sex.html}
   {$form.btnSubmit.html}
{$form.endtag}

When you add aradiobutton, the 4th parameter in the
addElement function is an arraywith the values (the
array keys) and the names of the values (the
arrayvalues). 
 
You also shouldn't put the radiobutton element twice
on thetemplate as that will give strange results.
 
Hope that makes it a little bit more clear.
 
cheers,
 
 
pieter

From pieter at yellowduck.be  Thu Mar 23 14:23:21 2006
From: pieter at yellowduck.be (Pieter Claerhout)
Date: Thu, 23 Mar 2006 14:23:21 +0100
Subject: [ydf-users] Re: Query Regarding menu
In-Reply-To: <20060323042503.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.c88a592b35.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
References: <20060323042503.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.c88a592b35.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
Message-ID: <4aef63030603230523j6ea29c77kccd1e51ca8d80af2@mail.gmail.com>

Take a look at this example:

The PHP code:


<?php

    // Standard include
    include_once( dirname( __FILE__ ) . '/../YDFramework2/YDF2_init.php' );

    // Includes
    YDInclude( 'YDForm.php' );
    YDInclude( 'YDTemplate.php' );

    // Class definition
    class form_checkboxgroup extends YDRequest {

        // Class constructor
        function form_checkboxgroup() {
            $this->YDRequest();
        }

        // Default action
        function actionDefault() {

            // Create the form
            $form = new YDForm( 'form1' );

            // Add the radiobutton
            $form->addElement( 'checkboxgroup', 'choose_multiple', 'Choose
multiple', array(), array( 0 => 'choice 1', 1 => 'choice 2' ) );

            // Add the submit button
            $form->addElement( 'submit', 'btnSubmit', 'submit' );

            // Set the defaults
            $form->setDefaults( array( 'choose_multiple' => array( 0=>0,
1=>1 ) ) );

            // Process the form
            if ( $form->validate() === true ) {
                YDDebugUtil::dump( $form->getValues() );
            }

            // Add the template
            $tpl = new YDTemplate();

            // Add the form to the template
            $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );

            // Display the template
            $tpl->display();

        }

    }

    // Process the request
    YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );

?>
The template:

{$form.tag}
    {$form.choose_multiple.html|@replace:'##ITEMSEP##':'<br/>'}
    <br/>
    {$form.btnSubmit.html}
{$form.endtag}


Cheers,


pieter

From dab214 at yahoo.com  Thu Mar 23 14:40:57 2006
From: dab214 at yahoo.com (dab)

Subject: [ydf-users] class structure question
In-Reply-To: <4aef63030603230523j6ea29c77kccd1e51ca8d80af2@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20060323134057.61450.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>

hi all,
what is the best way to make sure certain methods that
are used across the site are accesable from the main
class?
i'd like to access the methods without having to
initiating a new object, accessing it like it was a
method in the parent class.
the way i have it now is one class called Core that
inherits from YDRequest and all my classes inherits
from Core. Not a very good setup so i was hoping there
are better options.
thanks.

/dan


--- Pieter Claerhout <pieter at yellowduck.be> wrote:

> Take a look at this example:
> 
> The PHP code:
> 
> 
> <?php
> 
>     // Standard include
>     include_once( dirname( __FILE__ ) .
> '/../YDFramework2/YDF2_init.php' );
> 
>     // Includes
>     YDInclude( 'YDForm.php' );
>     YDInclude( 'YDTemplate.php' );
> 
>     // Class definition
>     class form_checkboxgroup extends YDRequest {
> 
>         // Class constructor
>         function form_checkboxgroup() {
>             $this->YDRequest();
>         }
> 
>         // Default action
>         function actionDefault() {
> 
>             // Create the form
>             $form = new YDForm( 'form1' );
> 
>             // Add the radiobutton
>             $form->addElement( 'checkboxgroup',
> 'choose_multiple', 'Choose
> multiple', array(), array( 0 => 'choice 1', 1 =>
> 'choice 2' ) );
> 
>             // Add the submit button
>             $form->addElement( 'submit',
> 'btnSubmit', 'submit' );
> 
>             // Set the defaults
>             $form->setDefaults( array(
> 'choose_multiple' => array( 0=>0,
> 1=>1 ) ) );
> 
>             // Process the form
>             if ( $form->validate() === true ) {
>                 YDDebugUtil::dump(
> $form->getValues() );
>             }
> 
>             // Add the template
>             $tpl = new YDTemplate();
> 
>             // Add the form to the template
>             $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );
> 
>             // Display the template
>             $tpl->display();
> 
>         }
> 
>     }
> 
>     // Process the request
>     YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );
> 
> ?>
> The template:
> 
> {$form.tag}
>    
>
{$form.choose_multiple.html|@replace:'##ITEMSEP##':'<br/>'}
>     <br/>
>     {$form.btnSubmit.html}
> {$form.endtag}
> 
> 
> Cheers,
> 
> 
> pieter
> 
>

From pieter at yellowduck.be  Thu Mar 23 14:58:57 2006
From: pieter at yellowduck.be (Pieter Claerhout)
Date: Thu, 23 Mar 2006 14:58:57 +0100
Subject: [ydf-users] class structure question
In-Reply-To: <20060323134057.61450.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <4aef63030603230523j6ea29c77kccd1e51ca8d80af2@mail.gmail.com>
	 <20060323134057.61450.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4aef63030603230558l319d0793ibed89761f19acd6b@mail.gmail.com>

Inheritance is the way to go. If you want to have common functionality
between the different requests, you extends YDRequest and implement it in
there.

Why do you dislike about this approach? I think it's a good programming
practice to use inheritence for this.

cheers,


pieter

> > multiple', array(), array( 0 => 'choice 1', 1 =>
> > 'choice 2' ) );
> >
> >             // Add the submit button
> >             $form->addElement( 'submit',
> > 'btnSubmit', 'submit' );
> >
> >             // Set the defaults
> >             $form->setDefaults( array(
> > 'choose_multiple' => array( 0=>0,
> > 1=>1 ) ) );
> >
> >             // Process the form
> >             if ( $form->validate() === true ) {
> >                 YDDebugUtil::dump(
> > $form->getValues() );
> >             }
> >
> >             // Add the template
> >             $tpl = new YDTemplate();
> >
> >             // Add the form to the template
> >             $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );
> >
> >             // Display the template
> >             $tpl->display();
> >
> >         }
> >
> >     }
> >
> >     // Process the request
> >     YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );
> >
> > ?>
> > The template:
> >
> > {$form.tag}
> >
> >
> {$form.choose_multiple.html|@replace:'##ITEMSEP##':'<br/>'}
> >     <br/>
> >     {$form.btnSubmit.html}
> > {$form.endtag}
> >
> >
> > Cheers,
> >
> >
> > pieter

--- Pieter Claerhout <pieter at yellowduck.be> wrote:

> Inheritance is the way to go. If you want to have
> common functionality
> between the different requests, you extends
> YDRequest and implement it in
> there.
> 
> Why do you dislike about this approach? I think it's
> a good programming
> practice to use inheritence for this.
> 
> cheers,
> 
> 
> pieter
> 
> On 3/23/06, dab <dab214 at yahoo.com> wrote:
> >
> > hi all,
> > what is the best way to make sure certain methods
> that
> > are used across the site are accesable from the
> main
> > class?
> > i'd like to access the methods without having to
> > initiating a new object, accessing it like it was
> a
> > method in the parent class.
> > the way i have it now is one class called Core
> that
> > inherits from YDRequest and all my classes
> inherits
> > from Core. Not a very good setup so i was hoping
> there
> > are better options.
> > thanks.
> >
> > /dan
> >
> >
> > --- Pieter Claerhout <pieter at yellowduck.be> wrote:
> >
> > > Take a look at this example:
> > >
> > > The PHP code:
> > >
> > >
> > > <?php
> > >
> > >     // Standard include
> > >     include_once( dirname( __FILE__ ) .
> > > '/../YDFramework2/YDF2_init.php' );
> > >
> > >     // Includes
> > >     YDInclude( 'YDForm.php' );
> > >     YDInclude( 'YDTemplate.php' );
> > >
> > >     // Class definition
> > >     class form_checkboxgroup extends YDRequest {
> > >
> > >         // Class constructor
> > >         function form_checkboxgroup() {
> > >             $this->YDRequest();
> > >         }
> > >
> > >         // Default action
> > >         function actionDefault() {
> > >
> > >             // Create the form
> > >             $form = new YDForm( 'form1' );
> > >
> > >             // Add the radiobutton
> > >             $form->addElement( 'checkboxgroup',
> > > 'choose_multiple', 'Choose
> > > multiple', array(), array( 0 => 'choice 1', 1 =>
> > > 'choice 2' ) );
> > >
> > >             // Add the submit button
> > >             $form->addElement( 'submit',
> > > 'btnSubmit', 'submit' );
> > >
> > >             // Set the defaults
> > >             $form->setDefaults( array(
> > > 'choose_multiple' => array( 0=>0,
> > > 1=>1 ) ) );
> > >
> > >             // Process the form
> > >             if ( $form->validate() === true ) {
> > >                 YDDebugUtil::dump(
> > > $form->getValues() );
> > >             }
> > >
> > >             // Add the template
> > >             $tpl = new YDTemplate();
> > >
> > >             // Add the form to the template
> > >             $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );
> > >
> > >             // Display the template
> > >             $tpl->display();
> > >
> > >         }
> > >
> > >     }
> > >
> > >     // Process the request
> > >     YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );
> > >
> > > ?>
> > > The template:
> > >
> > > {$form.tag}
> > >
> > >
> >
>
{$form.choose_multiple.html|@replace:'##ITEMSEP##':'<br/>'}
> > >     <br/>
> > >     {$form.btnSubmit.html}
> > > {$form.endtag}
> > >
> > >
> > > Cheers,
> > >
> > >
> > > pieter
> > >
> > >

> Take a look at this example:

> The PHP code:
>
> <?php
>     // Standard include
>     include_once( dirname( __FILE__ ) . '/../YDFramework2/YDF2_init.php'
> );
>     // Includes
>     YDInclude( 'YDForm.php' );
>     YDInclude( 'YDTemplate.php' );
>     // Class definition
>     class form_checkboxgroup extends YDRequest {
>         // Class constructor
>         function form_checkboxgroup() {
>             $this->YDRequest();
>         }
>         // Default action
>         function actionDefault() {
>             // Create the form
>             $form = new YDForm( 'form1' );
>             // Add the radiobutton
>             $form->addElement( 'checkboxgroup', 'choose_multiple', 'Choose
> multiple', array(), array( 0 => 'choice 1', 1 => 'choice 2' ) );
>             // Add the submit button
>             $form->addElement( 'submit', 'btnSubmit', 'submit' );
>             // Set the defaults
>             $form->setDefaults( array( 'choose_multiple' => array( 0=>0,
> 1=>1 ) ) );
>             // Process the form
>             if ( $form->validate() === true ) {
>                 YDDebugUtil::dump( $form->getValues() );
>             }
>             // Add the template
>             $tpl = new YDTemplate();
>             // Add the form to the template
>             $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );
>             // Display the template
>             $tpl->display();
>         }
>     }
>     // Process the request
>     YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );
> ?>
> The template:
>
> {$form.tag}
>     {$form.choose_multiple.html|@replace:'##ITEMSEP##':'<br/>'<%7B$form.choose_multiple.html%7C at replace:'#%23ITEMSEP%23%23':'%3Cbr/%3E'>
> }
>     <br/>
>     {$form.btnSubmit.html}
> {$form.endtag}

YDDatabase.php lines 1180 - 1210 are:


        function _logSql( $sql ) {

            // Split the SQL in different lines
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'SELECT', 'SELECT', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'UPDATE', 'UPDATE', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'DELETE', 'DELETE', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'INSERT', 'INSERT', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'FROM', YD_CRLF . 'FROM', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'INTO', YD_CRLF . 'INTO', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'VALUES', YD_CRLF . 'VALUES', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'LEFT JOIN', YD_CRLF . 'LEFT JOIN', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'RIGHT JOIN', YD_CRLF . 'RIGHT JOIN', $sql
);
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'INNER JOIN', YD_CRLF . 'INNER JOIN', $sql
);
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'WHERE', YD_CRLF . 'WHERE', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'ORDER BY', YD_CRLF . 'ORDER BY', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'GROUP BY', YD_CRLF . 'GROUP BY', $sql );
            $sql = str_ireplace( 'LIMIT', YD_CRLF . 'LIMIT', $sql );

            // Get the backtrace
            $trace = debug_backtrace();

            // Format the SQL
            $sql_final = '';
            foreach ( explode( YD_CRLF, $sql ) as $line ) {
                $sql_final .= '[' . $trace[2]['file'] . ':' .
$trace[2]['line'] . '] ' . $line . YD_CRLF;
            }

            // Add it to the query log
            array_push( $GLOBALS['YD_SQL_QUERY'], $sql_final );

        }

> > Dear Sir

> >
> >        While using *checkboxgroup *it gives the following error
> >
> > *Fatal error*: Unknown form element type "checkboxgroup" for element
> > "choose_multiple". in *D:\web\Moses\YDFramework2\YDClasses\YDForm.php*on line
> > *329 *
> >
> >       what is the solution.....
> >
> >
> > regards
> > moses
> >
> >
> >
> >
> >
> >
> >
> >
> >
> >
> >
> > Take a look at this example:
> >
> > The PHP code:
> >
> > <?php
> >     // Standard include
> >     include_once( dirname( __FILE__ ) . '/../YDFramework2/YDF2_init.php'
> > );
> >     // Includes
> >     YDInclude( 'YDForm.php' );
> >     YDInclude( 'YDTemplate.php' );
> >     // Class definition
> >     class form_checkboxgroup extends YDRequest {
> >         // Class constructor
> >         function form_checkboxgroup() {
> >             $this->YDRequest();
> >         }
> >         // Default action
> >         function actionDefault() {
> >             // Create the form
> >             $form = new YDForm( 'form1' );
> >             // Add the radiobutton
> >             $form->addElement( 'checkboxgroup', 'choose_multiple',
> > 'Choose multiple', array(), array( 0 => 'choice 1', 1 => 'choice 2' ) );
> >             // Add the submit button
> >             $form->addElement( 'submit', 'btnSubmit', 'submit' );
> >             // Set the defaults
> >             $form->setDefaults( array( 'choose_multiple' => array( 0=>0,
> > 1=>1 ) ) );
> >             // Process the form
> >             if ( $form->validate() === true ) {
> >                 YDDebugUtil::dump( $form->getValues() );
> >             }
> >             // Add the template
> >             $tpl = new YDTemplate();
> >             // Add the form to the template
> >             $tpl->assignForm ( 'form',$form );
> >             // Display the template
> >             $tpl->display();
> >         }
> >     }
> >     // Process the request
> >     YDInclude( 'YDF2_process.php' );
> > ?>
> > The template:
> >
> > {$form.tag}
> >     {$form.choose_multiple.html|@replace:'##ITEMSEP##':'<br/>'
> > <%7B$form.choose_multiple.html%7C at replace:'#%23ITEMSEP%23%23':'%3Cbr/%3E'>
> > }
> >     <br/>
> >     {$form.btnSubmit.html}
> > {$form.endtag}
> >
> >
> > Cheers,
> >
> >
> > pieter
> >
> >

> >         function _logSql( $sql ) {
> >
> >             // Split the SQL in different lines
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'SELECT', 'SELECT',
> > $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'UPDATE', 'UPDATE',
> > $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'DELETE', 'DELETE',
> > $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'INSERT', 'INSERT',
> > $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'FROM', YD_CRLF .
> > 'FROM', $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'INTO', YD_CRLF .
> > 'INTO', $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'VALUES', YD_CRLF .
> > 'VALUES', $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'LEFT JOIN',
> > YD_CRLF . 'LEFT JOIN', $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'RIGHT JOIN',
> > YD_CRLF . 'RIGHT JOIN', $sql
> > );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'INNER JOIN',
> > YD_CRLF . 'INNER JOIN', $sql
> > );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'WHERE', YD_CRLF .
> > 'WHERE', $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'ORDER BY', YD_CRLF
> > . 'ORDER BY', $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'GROUP BY', YD_CRLF
> > . 'GROUP BY', $sql );
> >             $sql = str_ireplace( 'LIMIT', YD_CRLF .
> > 'LIMIT', $sql );
> >
> >             // Get the backtrace
> >             $trace = debug_backtrace();
> >
> >             // Format the SQL
> >             $sql_final = '';
> >             foreach ( explode( YD_CRLF, $sql ) as
> > $line ) {
> >                 $sql_final .= '[' .
> > $trace[2]['file'] . ':' .
> > $trace[2]['line'] . '] ' . $line . YD_CRLF;
> >             }
> >
> >             // Add it to the query log
> >             array_push( $GLOBALS['YD_SQL_QUERY'],
> > $sql_final );
> >
> >         }
> > And that YDF2_core.php lines 416-429 read:

Hi Moses,

the validate function and therefor also the form rules only get checked when
a form is submitted. It basically checks if the $_POST array is populated or
not to see if the form values are submitted or not.

Have a look at the validate function in YDForm.php. The source code is
pretty straightforward for this part.

cheers,


pieter

From phmassa at gmail.com  Tue Mar 28 09:27:48 2006
From: phmassa at gmail.com (ph-m)
Date: Tue, 28 Mar 2006 09:27:48 +0200
Subject: [ydf-users] Ajax
Message-ID: <829084a60603272327y44836149oec2706bccff35fde@mail.gmail.com>

hi,

Since last releases, with ajax, I've lost styles, this is my code :

		function index() {

			$this->YDRequest();
			$this->tpl = new YDTemplate();
            $this->timer = new YDTimer();

		}


		// Default action
		function actionDefault() {

            $myform = new YDForm('myform');
			$myform->addElement( 'text', 'arg1', 'Nom :', array( 'maxlength' => 15 ) );
			$myform->addElement( 'button', 'mybutton', 'Interroger' );
			$myform->addElement( 'span', 'myspanresult', '&nbsp;' );

            $myform->addFilter( 'arg1', 'trim' );
            $myform->addRule( 'arg1', 'required', 'requis' );

			// create ajax object
			$this->ajax = new YDAjax( $this->tpl );
            $this->ajax->addForm( $myform );

            // create custom effects for waiting message
            $onStart = new YDAjaxEffect('', 'opacity', 'hide()', 0 );
            $onShow  = new YDAjaxEffect('', 'opacity', 'custom(0,1)', 0 );
            $onHide  = new YDAjaxEffect('', 'opacity', "toggle()" );

            // use waiting message with custom effects
            $this->ajax->useWaitingMessage( "<h2>&nbsp;Recherche en
cours ... &nbsp;<\/h2>", array(), $onStart, $onShow, $onHide );
            //$this->ajax->useWaitingMessage( );

            $this->ajax->addEvent( 'mybutton', array( & $this,
'compute' ), array('arg1') );

			$this->ajax->processEvents();

			// assign form and display template
			$this->tpl->assign( 'app_titre', 'Annuaire' );
			$this->tpl->assign( 'app_nom', 'Annuaire Local' );
			$this->tpl->assignForm( 'form',  $myform );
            $this->tpl->assign( 'timer', $this->timer->getElapsed() );
			$this->tpl->display();
		}

		// compute call invoked by ajax client
		function compute( $x ){

            $retour = "";
            if($x!="") {
                $strSQL = "SELECT ag_nom, ag_prenom, ag_tel FROM
agents WHERE ag_nom LIKE '" . $x . "%'";
                $db = YDDatabase::getInstance( 'mysql',
YDConfig::get('db_name'), YDConfig::get('db_user'),
YDConfig::get('db_pass'), YDConfig::get('db_host') );
                $retour = "";
                $res = $db->getRecords( $strSQL );
                if($res) {
                    $retour = "<table cellspacing=\"0\"
cellpadding=\"0\" border=\"0\"><tr><th class=\"adminRowL\"
width=\"40%\">Nom</th><th class=\"adminRowL\"
width=\"40%\">Pr?nom</th><th class=\"adminRowL\"
width=\"20%\">T?l?phone</th></tr>";
                    foreach ($res as $row )
                            $retour .= "<tr
onMouseOver=\"YDRowMouseOver(this);\"
onMouseOut=\"YDRowMouseOut(this);\"><td class=\"adminRowL\">".
$row['ag_nom'] . "</td><td class=\"adminRowL\">" . $row['ag_prenom'] .
"</td><td class=\"adminRowL\">" . $row['ag_tel']  ."</td></tr>";
                    $retour .= "</table>";
                } else
                    $retour .= "<table cellspacing=\"0\"
cellpadding=\"0\" border=\"0\"><tr><td>pas de
r?ponse</td></tr></table>";
            }

            // assign result to span
			$this->ajax->addResult( 'myspanresult', $retour );

			// return response to client browser
			return $this->ajax->processResults();
		}


From francisco at fusemail.com  Tue Mar 28 12:16:39 2006
From: francisco at fusemail.com (Francisco Azevedo)
Date: Tue, 28 Mar 2006 11:16:39 +0100
Subject: [ydf-users] Ajax
In-Reply-To: <829084a60603272327y44836149oec2706bccff35fde@mail.gmail.com>
References: <829084a60603272327y44836149oec2706bccff35fde@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <44290D07.2070805@fusemail.com>

hi ph-m

You cannot apply styles because you are adding html and applying slashes 
to it.. and you shouldn't.

When adding results, if that results are html strings, you must add the 
original html.

In your example you must *not* do:

  $retour = "<table cellspacing=\"0\"
  cellpadding=\"0\" border=\"0\"><tr><th class=\"adminRowL\"
  width=\"40%\">Nom</th><th class=\"adminRowL\"
  width=\"40%\">Pr?nom</th><th class=\"adminRowL\"
  width=\"20%\">T?l?phone</th></tr>";
                      foreach ($res as $row )
                              $retour .= "<tr
  onMouseOver=\"YDRowMouseOver(this);\"
  onMouseOut=\"YDRowMouseOut(this);\"><td class=\"adminRowL\">".
  $row['ag_nom'] . "</td><td class=\"adminRowL\">" . $row['ag_prenom'] .
  "</td><td class=\"adminRowL\">" . $row['ag_tel']  ."</td></tr>";
                      $retour .= "</table>";
                  } else
                      $retour .= "<table cellspacing=\"0\"
  cellpadding=\"0\" border=\"0\"><tr><td>pas de
  r?ponse</td></tr></table>";

but you *should* do:

  $retour = '<table cellspacing="0"
  cellpadding="0" border="0"><tr><th class="adminRowL"
  width="40%">Nom</th><th class="adminRowL"
  width="40%">Pr?nom</th><th class="adminRowL"
  width="20%">T?l?phone</th></tr>';
                      foreach ($res as $row )
                              $retour .= '<tr
  onMouseOver="YDRowMouseOver(this);"
  onMouseOut="YDRowMouseOut(this);"><td class="adminRowL">'.
  $row['ag_nom'] . '</td><td class="adminRowL">' . $row['ag_prenom'] .
  '</td><td class="adminRowL">' . $row['ag_tel']  .'</td></tr>';
                      $retour .= '</table>';
                  } else
                      $retour .= '<table cellspacing="0"
  cellpadding="0" border="0"><tr><td>pas de
  r?ponse</td></tr></table>';

Please try again using the original html string.

Francisco A

From francisco at fusemail.com  Wed Mar 29 11:31:19 2006

Date: Wed, 29 Mar 2006 10:31:19 +0100
Subject: [ydf-users] 2 ideas for checkboxgroup form element
Message-ID: <442A53E7.3000204@fusemail.com>

Hi all

What do you think of:

1- defining the html separator as a special attribute? This attribute 
would be only understand internally by checkboxgroup and not rendered in 
html. Then we could define a checkgroup like:

$form->addElement( 'checkboxgroup', 'name', 'label', array('separator' 
=> '<br />'), array( 0 => 'choice 1', 1 => 'choice 2' ) );

2- defining another special attribute for place where labels are placed. 
Currently all labels are placed on the right side but sometimes is 
useful on right.

Francisco A

From dab214 at yahoo.com  Fri Mar 31 09:05:13 2006
From: dab214 at yahoo.com (dab)
Date: Thu, 30 Mar 2006 23:05:13 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [ydf-users] Query Regarding YDConfig
In-Reply-To: <20060330230719.fe477b357a56c857c15a39baa2ae95d5.47f0136808.wbe@email.email.secureserver.net>
Message-ID: <20060331070513.56161.qmail@web50209.mail.yahoo.com>

1. changing a YDFramework config variable.
2. it changes a YDFramework config variable.
3. when we wanna change a YDFramework config variable.

the code you pasted is just an example. here's a real
life one:
YDConfig::set( 'YD_DBOBJECT_PREFIX', 'db_' );

it add's a prefix on the database classes.

i could be wrong on this but i think the YDConfig is
just for YDFramework config variables and not your own
defined ones. 

/dan
